The\n340: \t\t\t// concern is that we might, in some future release, want\n341: \t\t\t// different behavior than is implemented now. One of the\n342: \t\t\t// hardest questions is how does an operator roll out the\n343: \t\t\t// new release in a cluster with multiple kube-apiservers\n344: \t\t\t// --- in a way that works no matter what servers crash\n345: \t\t\t// and restart when. If this handler reacts only to\n346: \t\t\t// changes in Spec then we have a scenario in which the\n347: \t\t\t// rollout leaves the old Status in place. The scenario\n348: \t\t\t// ends with this subsequence: deploy the last new server\n349: \t\t\t// before deleting the last old server, and in between\n350: \t\t\t// those two operations the last old server crashes and\n351: \t\t\t// recovers. The chosen solution is making this controller\n352: \t\t\t// insist on maintaining the particular state that it\n353: \t\t\t// establishes.\n354: \t\t\tif !(apiequality.Semantic.DeepEqual(oldFS.Spec, newFS.Spec) &&\n355: \t\t\t\tapiequality.Semantic.DeepEqual(oldFS.Status, newFS.Status)) {\n356: \t\t\t\tklog.V(7).Infof(\"Triggered API priority and fairness config reloading in %s due to spec and/or status update of FS %s\", cfgCtlr.name, newFS.Name)\n357: \t\t\t\tcfgCtlr.configQueue.Add(0)\n358: \t\t\t} else {\n359: \t\t\t\tklog.V(7).Infof(\"No trigger of API priority and fairness config reloading in %s due to spec and status non-change of FS %s\", cfgCtlr.name, newFS.Name)\n360: \t\t\t}\n361: \t\t},\n362: \t\tDeleteFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n363: \t\t\tname, _ := cache.DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)\n364: \t\t\tklog.V(7).Infof(\"Triggered API priority and fairness config reloading in %s due to deletion of FS %s\", cfgCtlr.name, name)\n365: \t\t\tcfgCtlr.configQueue.Add(0)\n366: \n367: \t\t}})\n368: \treturn cfgCtlr\n369: }\n370: \n371: func (cfgCtlr *configController) Run(stopCh <-chan struct{}) error {\n372: \tdefer utilruntime.HandleCrash()\n373: \n374: \t// Let the config worker stop when we are done\n375: \tdefer cfgCtlr.configQueue.ShutDown()\n376: \n377: \tklog.Info(\"Starting API Priority and Fairness config controller\")\n378: \tif ok := cache.WaitForCacheSync(stopCh, cfgCtlr.plInformerSynced, cfgCtlr.fsInformerSynced); !ok {\n379: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"Never achieved initial sync\")\n380: \t}\n381: \n382: \tklog.Info(\"Running API Priority and Fairness config worker\")\n383: \tgo wait.Until(cfgCtlr.runWorker, time.Second, stopCh)\n384: \n385: \tklog.Info(\"Running API Priority and Fairness periodic rebalancing process\")\n386: \tgo wait.Until(cfgCtlr.updateBorrowing, borrowingAdjustmentPeriod, stopCh)\n387: \n388: \t<-stopCh\n389: \tklog.Info(\"Shutting down API Priority and Fairness config worker\")\n390: \treturn nil\n391: }\n392: \n393: func (cfgCtlr *configController) updateBorrowing() {\n394: \tcfgCtlr.lock.Lock()\n395: \tdefer cfgCtlr.lock.Unlock()\n396: \tcfgCtlr.updateBorrowingLocked(true, cfgCtlr.priorityLevelStates)\n397: }\n398: \n399: func (cfgCtlr *configController) updateBorrowingLocked(setCompleters bool, plStates map[string]*priorityLevelState) {\n400: \titems := make([]allocProblemItem, 0, len(plStates))\n401: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes@7ae9c0d83a91bc9c7e35665665e662152fa39d13/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go%3FL300-400"}}}

\"## Rate Limiting Implementation Patterns in Envoy and Kubernetes\\n\\n### Envoy Rate Limiting Architecture\\n\\nEnvoy implements rate limiting at three distinct filter levels:\\n\\n**1. HTTP Local Rate Limit Filter**\\nThe HTTP local rate limit filter (source/extensions/filters/http/local_ratelimit/) implements per-request rate limiting using a token bucket algorithm. The FilterConfig class in local_ratelimit.h manages configuration of token bucket parameters (max_tokens, fill_interval, tokens_per_fill). The implementation supports both global and per-connection rate limiting modes controlled by the `local_rate_limit_per_downstream_connection` configuration parameter.\\n\\n**2. Token Bucket Implementation**\\nThe actual token bucket mechanism is implemented in source/extensions/filters/common/local_ratelimit/local_ratelimit_impl.h through the LocalRateLimiterImpl and RateLimitTokenBucket classes. This design separates the common rate limiting logic from filter-specific configuration, allowing token buckets to be reused across listener, network, and HTTP filters. The implementation includes support for dynamic descriptors using an LRU cache (DynamicDescriptor and DynamicDescriptorMap classes).\\n\\n**3. Global Rate Limit Service Client (Rate Limit Quota Service)**\\nEnvoy provides a distributed rate limiting solution through the Rate Limit Quota Service (RLQS) protocol implemented in source/extensions/filters/http/rate_limit_quota/. The GlobalRateLimitClientImpl class (global_client_impl.h/cc) handles bidirectional gRPC streaming with the RLQS server, managing quota buckets across worker threads. The LocalRateLimitClientImpl (client_impl.h/cc) provides per-worker thread access to the global rate limit client via thread-local storage. The quota bucket cache (quota_bucket_cache.h) stores quota information and coordinates between the global and local clients.\\n\\n**4. Network and Listener Level Filters**\\nEnvoy also provides rate limiting at the network (source/extensions/filters/network/local_ratelimit/) and listener (source/extensions/filters/listener/local_ratelimit/) levels, allowing rate limiting to be applied before HTTP processing or even before TLS handshake, using the same token bucket implementation pattern.\\n\\n### Kubernetes Rate Limiting Architecture\\n\\n**1. Token Bucket Rate Limiter (Client-Side)**\\nKubernetes client-go library implements a token bucket rate limiter in staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/flowcontrol/throttle.go. The NewTokenBucketRateLimiter function wraps the golang.org/x/time/rate.Limiter to provide a rate limiter that allows burst traffic while maintaining a smooth QPS. The tokenBucketRateLimiter struct wraps rate.Limiter and adds clock support for testability.\\n\\n**2. API Priority and Fairness (APF) Controller**\\nThe Kubernetes API server implements sophisticated priority and fairness handling through the APF controller in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go. The configController class watches FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration objects from the flowcontrol API group. The controller manages priorityLevelState objects for each priority level, implementing dynamic borrowing of concurrency capacity between priority levels through the updateBorrowing method called periodically every 10 seconds.\\n\\n**3. Fair Queuing Implementation**\\nThe core queueing logic is implemented in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/, implementing the fair queuing for server requests technique. The queueSet class maintains separate queues for each flow schema, tracking virtual finish times and seats (concurrency units) using virtual clock calculations. This ensures fair resource allocation across different priority levels and flow schemas.\\n\\n**4. Priority Level Configuration**\\nPriority levels are defined in staging/src/k8s.io/api/flowcontrol/v1/types.go and related versioned API types. Each PriorityLevelConfiguration specifies whether requests are exempt from limits (PriorityLevelEnablementExempt) or subject to concurrency limits (PriorityLevelEnablementLimited), with nominalConcurrencyShares controlling the fair share allocation.\\n\\n**5. APF Filter**\\nThe apf_filter.go implements the HTTP filter that integrates APF with the HTTP request handling pipeline. The filter classifies incoming requests based on FlowSchema rules, dispatching them to the appropriate priority level queue, and ensuring proper waiting and execution handling.\\n\\n### Key Differences in Patterns\\n\\n**Envoy's approach:**\\n- Uses token bucket as the primary mechanism at all levels\\n- Supports distributed rate limiting via gRPC streaming to a centralized service\\n- Separates local (per-connection/process) and global (distributed) rate limiting\\n- Token buckets are configurable with fill intervals and tokens per fill\\n\\n**Kubernetes' approach:**\\n- Combines token bucket with sophisticated fair queuing for multi-tenant scenarios\\n- Implements priority-based scheduling with dynamic capacity borrowing\\n- Tracks per-request work estimates and concurrency consumption\\n- Uses virtual clock calculations for fair allocation of limited concurrency\\n\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":4284,"cache_read_input_tokens":98168,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":4284},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"f248c97b-3643-4c81-9c5b-6cb2cde87390","uuid":"0a040857-29c1-4ab2-a054-ef5363135af6"}

\"symbol\": \"queueSet\"\n   231→    }\n   232→  ],\n   233→  \"text\": \"## Rate Limiting Implementation Patterns in Envoy and Kubernetes\\n\\n### Envoy Rate Limiting Architecture\\n\\nEnvoy implements rate limiting at three distinct filter levels:\\n\\n**1. HTTP Local Rate Limit Filter**\\nThe HTTP local rate limit filter (source/extensions/filters/http/local_ratelimit/) implements per-request rate limiting using a token bucket algorithm. The FilterConfig class in local_ratelimit.h manages configuration of token bucket parameters (max_tokens, fill_interval, tokens_per_fill). The implementation supports both global and per-connection rate limiting modes controlled by the `local_rate_limit_per_downstream_connection` configuration parameter.\\n\\n**2. Token Bucket Implementation**\\nThe actual token bucket mechanism is implemented in source/extensions/filters/common/local_ratelimit/local_ratelimit_impl.h through the LocalRateLimiterImpl and RateLimitTokenBucket classes. This design separates the common rate limiting logic from filter-specific configuration, allowing token buckets to be reused across listener, network, and HTTP filters. The implementation includes support for dynamic descriptors using an LRU cache (DynamicDescriptor and DynamicDescriptorMap classes).\\n\\n**3. Global Rate Limit Service Client (Rate Limit Quota Service)**\\nEnvoy provides a distributed rate limiting solution through the Rate Limit Quota Service (RLQS) protocol implemented in source/extensions/filters/http/rate_limit_quota/. The GlobalRateLimitClientImpl class (global_client_impl.h/cc) handles bidirectional gRPC streaming with the RLQS server, managing quota buckets across worker threads. The LocalRateLimitClientImpl (client_impl.h/cc) provides per-worker thread access to the global rate limit client via thread-local storage. The quota bucket cache (quota_bucket_cache.h) stores quota information and coordinates between the global and local clients.\\n\\n**4. Network and Listener Level Filters**\\nEnvoy also provides rate limiting at the network (source/extensions/filters/network/local_ratelimit/) and listener (source/extensions/filters/listener/local_ratelimit/) levels, allowing rate limiting to be applied before HTTP processing or even before TLS handshake, using the same token bucket implementation pattern.\\n\\n### Kubernetes Rate Limiting Architecture\\n\\n**1. Token Bucket Rate Limiter (Client-Side)**\\nKubernetes client-go library implements a token bucket rate limiter in staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/flowcontrol/throttle.go. The NewTokenBucketRateLimiter function wraps the golang.org/x/time/rate.Limiter to provide a rate limiter that allows burst traffic while maintaining a smooth QPS. The tokenBucketRateLimiter struct wraps rate.Limiter and adds clock support for testability.\\n\\n**2. API Priority and Fairness (APF) Controller**\\nThe Kubernetes API server implements sophisticated priority and fairness handling through the APF controller in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go. The configController class watches FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration objects from the flowcontrol API group. The controller manages priorityLevelState objects for each priority level, implementing dynamic borrowing of concurrency capacity between priority levels through the updateBorrowing method called periodically every 10 seconds.\\n\\n**3. Fair Queuing Implementation**\\nThe core queueing logic is implemented in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/, implementing the fair queuing for server requests technique. The queueSet class maintains separate queues for each flow schema, tracking virtual finish times and seats (concurrency units) using virtual clock calculations. This ensures fair resource allocation across different priority levels and flow schemas.\\n\\n**4. Priority Level Configuration**\\nPriority levels are defined in staging/src/k8s.io/api/flowcontrol/v1/types.go and related versioned API types. Each PriorityLevelConfiguration specifies whether requests are exempt from limits (PriorityLevelEnablementExempt) or subject to concurrency limits (PriorityLevelEnablementLimited), with nominalConcurrencyShares controlling the fair share allocation.\\n\\n**5. APF Filter**\\nThe apf_filter.go implements the HTTP filter that integrates APF with the HTTP request handling pipeline. The filter classifies incoming requests based on FlowSchema rules, dispatching them to the appropriate priority level queue, and ensuring proper waiting and execution handling.\\n\\n### Key Differences in Patterns\\n\\n**Envoy's approach:**\\n- Uses token bucket as the primary mechanism at all levels\\n- Supports distributed rate limiting via gRPC streaming to a centralized service\\n- Separates local (per-connection/process) and global (distributed) rate limiting\\n- Token buckets are configurable with fill intervals and tokens per fill\\n\\n**Kubernetes' approach:**\\n- Combines token bucket with sophisticated fair queuing for multi-tenant scenarios\\n- Implements priority-based scheduling with dynamic capacity borrowing\\n- Tracks per-request work estimates and concurrency consumption\\n- Uses virtual clock calculations for fair allocation of limited concurrency\\n\"\n   234→}\n   235→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. \"## Rate Limiting Implementation Patterns in Envoy and Kubernetes\\n\\n### Envoy Rate Limiting Architecture\\n\\nEnvoy implements rate limiting at three distinct filter levels:\\n\\n**1. HTTP Local Rate Limit Filter**\\nThe HTTP local rate limit filter (source/extensions/filters/http/local_ratelimit/) implements per-request rate limiting using a token bucket algorithm. The FilterConfig class in local_ratelimit.h manages configuration of token bucket parameters (max_tokens, fill_interval, tokens_per_fill). The implementation supports both global and per-connection rate limiting modes controlled by the `local_rate_limit_per_downstream_connection` configuration parameter.\\n\\n**2. Token Bucket Implementation**\\nThe actual token bucket mechanism is implemented in source/extensions/filters/common/local_ratelimit/local_ratelimit_impl.h through the LocalRateLimiterImpl and RateLimitTokenBucket classes. This design separates the common rate limiting logic from filter-specific configuration, allowing token buckets to be reused across listener, network, and HTTP filters. The implementation includes support for dynamic descriptors using an LRU cache (DynamicDescriptor and DynamicDescriptorMap classes).\\n\\n**3. Global Rate Limit Service Client (Rate Limit Quota Service)**\\nEnvoy provides a distributed rate limiting solution through the Rate Limit Quota Service (RLQS) protocol implemented in source/extensions/filters/http/rate_limit_quota/. The GlobalRateLimitClientImpl class (global_client_impl.h/cc) handles bidirectional gRPC streaming with the RLQS server, managing quota buckets across worker threads. The LocalRateLimitClientImpl (client_impl.h/cc) provides per-worker thread access to the global rate limit client via thread-local storage. The quota bucket cache (quota_bucket_cache.h) stores quota information and coordinates between the global and local clients.\\n\\n**4. Network and Listener Level Filters**\\nEnvoy also provides rate limiting at the network (source/extensions/filters/network/local_ratelimit/) and listener (source/extensions/filters/listener/local_ratelimit/) levels, allowing rate limiting to be applied before HTTP processing or even before TLS handshake, using the same token bucket implementation pattern.\\n\\n### Kubernetes Rate Limiting Architecture\\n\\n**1. Token Bucket Rate Limiter (Client-Side)**\\nKubernetes client-go library implements a token bucket rate limiter in staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/flowcontrol/throttle.go. The NewTokenBucketRateLimiter function wraps the golang.org/x/time/rate.Limiter to provide a rate limiter that allows burst traffic while maintaining a smooth QPS. The tokenBucketRateLimiter struct wraps rate.Limiter and adds clock support for testability.\\n\\n**2. API Priority and Fairness (APF) Controller**\\nThe Kubernetes API server implements sophisticated priority and fairness handling through the APF controller in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go. The configController class watches FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration objects from the flowcontrol API group. The controller manages priorityLevelState objects for each priority level, implementing dynamic borrowing of concurrency capacity between priority levels through the updateBorrowing method called periodically every 10 seconds.\\n\\n**3. Fair Queuing Implementation**\\nThe core queueing logic is implemented in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/, implementing the fair queuing for server requests technique. The queueSet class maintains separate queues for each flow schema, tracking virtual finish times and seats (concurrency units) using virtual clock calculations. This ensures fair resource allocation across different priority levels and flow schemas.\\n\\n**4. Priority Level Configuration**\\nPriority levels are defined in staging/src/k8s.io/api/flowcontrol/v1/types.go and related versioned API types. Each PriorityLevelConfiguration specifies whether requests are exempt from limits (PriorityLevelEnablementExempt) or subject to concurrency limits (PriorityLevelEnablementLimited), with nominalConcurrencyShares controlling the fair share allocation.\\n\\n**5. APF Filter**\\nThe apf_filter.go implements the HTTP filter that integrates APF with the HTTP request handling pipeline. The filter classifies incoming requests based on FlowSchema rules, dispatching them to the appropriate priority level queue, and ensuring proper waiting and execution handling.\\n\\n### Key Differences in Patterns\\n\\n**Envoy's approach:**\\n- Uses token bucket as the primary mechanism at all levels\\n- Supports distributed rate limiting via gRPC streaming to a centralized service\\n- Separates local (per-connection/process) and global (distributed) rate limiting\\n- Token buckets are configurable with fill intervals and tokens per fill\\n\\n**Kubernetes' approach:**\\n- Combines token bucket with sophisticated fair queuing for multi-tenant scenarios\\n- Implements priority-based scheduling with dynamic capacity borrowing\\n- Tracks per-request work estimates and concurrency consumption\\n- Uses virtual clock calculations for fair allocation of limited concurrency\\n\"\n}\n","numLines":235,"startLine":1,"totalLines":235}}}
